## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / continuous-time population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating a continuous-time population growth model. Typical relationships encode density dependence (crowding), time-varying environments (seasonality), and external inputs/harvest that modify the per-capita growth rate.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita growth)
- Linear birth–death with immigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (net growth plus constant stocking/immigration)
- Quadratic crowding (self-limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent reduction in growth)
- Verhulst logistic ODE (density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity-like saturation with c1 ≈ 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (logarithmic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases ~log(P))
- Richards / generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (adds shape parameter to logistic-like saturation)
- Strong Allee effect (cubic growth): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (low-density suppression + high-density crowding)
- Weak Allee effect (Allee-modified logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P + 1) (facilitation at low density without strict threshold)
- Constant-yield harvesting with growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (harvest/removal approximately constant in time)
- Proportional harvesting with growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest/removal proportional to population size)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affecting intrinsic growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P across all P, the system is near exponential growth/decay (constant per-capita rate).
- If dP_dt vs P is a concave-down parabola with zeros at P≈0 and P≈K, it indicates logistic-type density dependence (crowding-limited growth).
- If per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) decreases roughly linearly with P, a quadratic term in dP_dt (−c*P**2) is suggested.
- If per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P), Gompertz structure dP_dt ∝ P*log(K/P) is suggested.
- If dP_dt becomes negative at low P but positive at intermediate P (bistability/threshold), include an Allee factor like (c*P−1) multiplying P.
- If growth declines more sharply (or more gently) than logistic near high P, use a theta-logistic or Richards exponent to adjust curvature.
- If dP_dt shows a persistent offset even when P≈0, include a constant term (immigration/stocking) in dP_dt.
- If the time series shows periodic modulation in growth at similar P levels, include explicit t-periodic forcing in coefficients (e.g., c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)).
- If increasing removal pressure is suspected without additional covariates, model it as either constant removal (−c) or proportional removal (−c*P) added to a growth term.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG17)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6
Candidate formulas: 87

GT depends **only on \(P\)** (no \(t\)) and has the form
\[
0.768873878858443\;(-1+P/8.6703748695)(1-P/14.3328552381)P\;+\;0.768873878858443\;P^{1/3}.
\]
So GT is a sum of:
- a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (expand: it is \(aP + bP^2 + dP^3\) with fixed nonzero coefficients), plus
- a **fractional power term** \(kP^{1/3}\) with \(k\neq 0\).

Therefore any matching candidate must be able (by parameter choice) to produce **exactly** “(cubic polynomial) + (constant)\(P^{1/3}\)” and **nothing else** (no logs/exp/sin/sqrt/rational denominators unless they can be eliminated without killing needed terms).

### 1
